Job (variant file)

unicode hypertext edition: November, 2005, by Christopher McCartney

-Text and Textual Variants for the Old Greek Book of  Job  (Poetic): electronic edition (ca 1996).

-Public Domain Center for Computer Assisted Tools for Septuagint Studies (CATSS) edition prepared at the University of Pennsylvania, Center for Computer Analysis of Texts (CCAT)
-Filesize uncompressed: about ?? K
-Center for Computer Analysis of Texts (Robert A. Kraft)
Logan Hall, University of Pennsylvania,
Philadelphia PA 19104-6304 USA; kraft@ccat.sas.upenn.edu

-Bible:OldGreek:Poetic:Job (032)

This material was prepared by Gil Renberg, based on Septuaginta: Vetus Testamentum Graecum auctoritate Societatis Litterarum Gottingensis editum, vol. 11.4, Iob, ed. Joseph Ziegler (Goettingen: Vandenhoeck & Ruprecht, 1982), supplemented with more recent information or discoveries where available.

-File format is described by Robert Kraft, "Treatment of the Greek Textual Variants"
in Computer Assisted Tools for Septuagint Studies (CATSS), vol. 1: Ruth, Septuagint and Cognate Studies 20 (Scholars Press, 1986).
-Categories of variants are marked thus --
">" = lacking in the following witnesses,
"+" = longer text,
":" = alternative reading,
transpositions are treated as plus/minus readings, with "~" added
@@@ indicates indentation in the published text
<it>...</> indicates italics [which can now be indicated in html],
and <lt>...</> indicates Latin words and phrases [change now to italics];
for the Greek transliterations, TLG "Beta Code" has been used.
-Text divisions are marked by "~" at left margin, followed by "a" to designate the book, "x" for chapter, and "y" for verse; explicit numbers have been added for the user's convenience -- thus "~x2y5" = chapter 2, verse 5 [which now needs to be simplified].

This is the penultimate draft of the text and variants file for Greek LXX/OG Job, edited by Benjamin Dunning (11 Jan 1995) and Gil Renberg (summer 1996). Many editorial queries and calls for verification or correction remain in the file (in bold type) [update: the bold font did not survive the transition to unicode (see the "beta" version) -- Chris McCartney], but rather than hold this material back from circulation until there is time to edit it more fully, we hereby make it available with this warning about its unfinished character.

[[Renberg notes, need to do or check:

There are three types of apostrophes/single-quotes used in the app.crit.  These are the characters I am using to represent them:
      ’ or ‘      (Single-quote mark, will become ' once file is converted to text format)
                    Represents the most common of the three, the straight quote mark that tilts slightly
                     forwards, used for witnesses such as 534' and 46'
      `             (Key in upper right of keyboard, under tilde)
                    Represents the straight quote mark that tilts slightly backwards, as in L’`
      !             Represents the rounded single-quote, as in L’ and <it>lI</>’


Look (Ctrl-F) for each #-sign. I’m not sure what they mean or how to handle them. [Presumably "Theodotionic" text, supplementing the OG?]
#13 indicates hexaplaric asterisk (Theodotionic text)
Look at each occurrence of “cf” because sometimes when dealing with a variant that has “cf” it might not be necessary to use “cf” for each addition and deletion in that variant. [Usually means that something unusual is going on in the witness, such as abbreviation, or damaged reading]

Another possible problem is witnesses such as <it>C</>{1-147}, which is how it appears in the app.crit. <it>C</> includes 147 as a manuscript, so I have done it: <it>C</>{1}{-147}. If this isn’t right, it needs to be changed throughout for C{1}, C{2} and C{3}. [Seems to mean subgroups of italic C -- check the introduction!]

What is (2{o}), as in “Ol (2{o})”? And (1{o})? [2nd occurrence of that word in the verse] ]]
